Two Opinions on 'Yad' in the Verse of Creation
Razi presents two scholarly opinions on the meaning of 'yad' in the creation of Adam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two major scholarly opinions on the meaning of 'yad' (hand) in Q. 38:75 and the key arguments used to support each view.

Core Idea
The meaning of 'yad' in the Quran is debated: is it a real attribute or simply power?

In this passage, Imam al-Razi presents two competing interpretations of the phrase 'bi-yadayya' (with My two hands) from the verse about Adam's creation. The first opinion holds that 'hands' are real, distinct attributes of Allah, while the second reduces them to a metaphor for power. Razi lays out the proofs for each side, giving us a clear picture of the theological stakes involved in the debate over divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice Razi's structure: he states the two opinions, then lists proofs for the first, then begins the second.
The passage cuts off mid-sentence; just work with what is given.
2
Identify the first opinion and its three proofs
The first opinion says 'yad' are real attributes. Its three proofs are: (1) if 'yad' were power, all creation would be honored equally; (2) power is one but 'yad' is dual; (3) specification of Adam implies exclusivity, so 'yad' is not power. Make sure you understand each proof.
3
Examine the second opinion and its first proof
The second opinion says 'yad' is power. The first proof given is that the definition of power (ability to create) matches what 'yad' does. The second proof (about power's attachment) is cut off, so focus on the first.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this debate matters. If 'yad' is a real attribute, it implies a more literal understanding of divine attributes. If it is power, it avoids anthropomorphism. Note that Razi presents both sides without a final verdict.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله تعالى: «ما منعك أن تسجد لما خلقت بيدي» فنقول: للعلماء فيه قولان: القول الأول: إن اليدين صفتان قائمتان بذات الله تعالى. يحصل بهما التخلق على وجه التكريم والاصطفاء، كما في حق آدم عليه السلام. واحتج القائلون بهذا الوجه بوجوه: الأول: إن قوله تعالى: «ما منعك أن تسجد لما خلقت بيدي» مشعر بأنه تعالى إنما جعل آدم مسجودا للملائكة، لأنه تعالى خلقه بيديه. فلو كانت اليد عبارة عن القدرة، لكانت علة هذه المسجودية حاصلة في كل المخلوقات، فوجب هذا الحكم في الكل. وحيث لم يحصل، علمنا أن اليد صفة سوى القدرة. والثاني: إن قدرة الله تعالى واحدة، واليد موصوفة بالتثنية. والثالث: إن قوله تعالى: «لما خلقت بيدي» يدل على كونه مخصوصا بأنه مخلوق، والتخصيص بالذكر يدل على نفي الحكم عما عداه. فوجب في كل من سوى آدم عليه السلام أن لا يكونوا مخلوقين باليدين، ولا يشك في أنهم مخلوقون بالقدرة. وذلك يقتضي أن تكون اليد شيئا سوى القدرة. والقول الثاني: إن اليد ههنا هي القدرة. ويدل عليه وجوه: الأول: إن القدرة عبارة عن الصفة التي يكون الموصوف بها متمكنا من الإيجاد والتكوين، ونقل الشيء من العدم إلى الوجود. ولما كان المسمى باليد كذلك، كان ذلك المعنى نفس القدرة. والثاني: إن قدرة الله تعالى صفة قديمة، واجبة الوجود، فيجب تعلقها بكل ما يصح أن يكون مقدورا. وإلا لزم افتقارها في ذلك الاختصاص إلى المخصص. لكن المخصص
And as for His statement, the Exalted: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands?' – we say: There are two sayings for the scholars about it. The first saying: The two hands are two attributes subsisting in the essence of Allah, the Exalted. By them, creation occurs in the manner of honor and selection, as in the case of Adam, peace be upon him. Those who hold this view argued with proofs: The first: His statement, the Exalted: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands' indicates that the Exalted only made Adam prostrated to by the angels because He created him with His two hands. So if 'hand' were an expression for power, the cause of this being worthy of prostration would be present in all creatures, so this ruling would be necessary for all. But since it is not the case, we know that 'hand' is an attribute other than power. The second: The power of Allah, the Exalted, is one, but 'hand' is described with duality. The third: His statement, the Exalted: 'what I created with My two hands' indicates that he is specified as being created, and specification by mention indicates negation of the ruling from what is other than it. So it is necessary for everyone other than Adam, peace be upon him, that they are not created with two hands, and there is no doubt that they are created with power. And that necessitates that 'hand' be something other than power. The second saying: 'Hand' here is power. And it is indicated by proofs: The first: Power is the attribute by which the one described is able to bring into existence and create, and to transfer a thing from non-existence to existence. Since what is called 'hand' is like that, that meaning is power itself. The second: The power of Allah, the Exalted, is an eternal attribute, necessarily existent, so its attachment to everything that can be an object of power is necessary. Otherwise, its specificity in that attribution would require a specificr. But the specificr...
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents two scholarly opinions on the meaning of 'yad' in the verse 'ma mana'aka an tasjuda li-ma khalaqtu bi-yadayya' (Q. 38:75). The first opinion holds that 'the two hands' are two real attributes subsisting in Allah's essence, by which He created Adam specifically for honor. The proponents give three proofs: 1) If 'hand' meant power, then all creatures would be equally honored, but only Adam is honored; therefore 'hand' must be a distinct attribute. 2) God's power is one (singular), but hands are described with duality (tathniyah), indicating they are not the same as power. 3) The specification 'with My two hands' shows exclusivity; since other creatures are not created with two hands, 'hand' must be something other than power. The second opinion says 'hand' here is simply power (qudrah). Its evidence includes: 1) The definition of power (ability to create and bring into existence) matches what 'hand' does. 2) God's power is eternal and must apply to all possible objects; if it were restricted, it would need a specifier (mukhassis). The text cuts off during this second proof, leaving the argument incomplete.

Checkpoint
According to the first opinion, what is the third proof that 'yad' is not power?
A) Power is one, but 'hand' is dual.
B) If 'hand' were power, all creation would be honored.
C) The specification of Adam with 'bi-yadayya' implies exclusivity, so 'hand' must be special.
D) The definition of power matches the function of 'hand'.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Razi presents two competing interpretations of 'yad' in the creation verse, one seeing them as real attributes and the other as a metaphor for power, each supported by rational arguments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quranic verse about Adam being created with 'two hands', does your heart feel the honor and special status Allah gave to humanity? How does that honor change the way you treat yourself and others?
?
Al-Razi presents two opinions with rational proofs. Do you take the time to understand differing scholarly views on matters of faith, or do you quickly pick one without examining the arguments? What would it take for you to engage with difficult theological questions?
?
The passage shows that both opinions rely on reason and scripture. When your intellect leads you to a conclusion that seems to conflict with a literal reading of the Quran, do you trust your reason or dismiss it? How can you ensure your reasoning is guided by faith?

The First Opinion: Hands as Real Attributes
Razi states the first interpretation of 'hands' and gives three proofs for it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first interpretation of God's 'hands' in the Qur'an and the three scriptural proofs that support it.

Core Idea
God's hands are real attributes, not metaphors—proven by the verses themselves.

The verse 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands?' has sparked theological debate. Some scholars argue that 'hands' are real attributes that honor Adam specially. Three proofs from the text itself support this view. Let's examine them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the first opinion
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Razi presents the first opinion: the two hands are real attributes subsisting in God's essence, by which He created Adam as an honor.
2
Analyze the first proof
The first proof argues that if 'hand' meant power, then all creatures would be equally worthy of prostration, but only Adam is singled out. Therefore, 'hand' must be an attribute other than power.
This proof relies on the universality of power vs. the specificity of the verse.
3
Examine the second proof
The second proof notes that God's power is one, but the word 'hand' appears in dual form (two hands). This indicates a distinction between power and hands.
Duality implies multiplicity, while power is singular.
4
Consider the third proof
The third proof uses the principle that specification by mention negates the ruling from others. Since Adam is specified as being created with two hands, others are not. Yet they are created with power, so hands cannot be power.
This is a linguistic argument from the form of the verse.
5
Reflect on the implications
Think about what this means for divine attributes: if hands are real, they are distinct from power and have a special role in creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله تعالى: «ما منعك أن تسجد لما خلقت بيدى (١٤) فنقول: للعلماء فيه قولان: القول الأول: إن اليدين صفتان قائمتان بذات الله تعالى. يحصل بهما التخلق على وجه التكريم والاصطفاء، كما في حق آدم عليه السلام. واحتج القائلون بهذا الوجه بوجوه: الأول: إن قوله تعالى: «ما منعك أن تسجد لما خلقت بيدي» مشعر بأنه تعالى إنما جعل آدم مسجوداً للملائكه، لأنه تعالى خلقه بيديه. فلو كانت اليد عبارة عن القدرة، لكانت علة هذه المسجودية حاصلة في كل المخلوقات، فوجب هذا الحكم في الكل. وحيث لم يحصل، علمنا أن اليد صفة سوى القدرة. والثاني: إن قدرة الله تعالى واحدة، واليد موصوفة بالتثنية. والثالث: إن قوله (تعالى) (١٥): «لما خلقت بيدي» يدل على كونه مخصوصاً بأنه مخلوق، والتخصيص بالذكر يدل على نفي الحكم عما عداه. فوجب في كل من سوى آدم عليه السلام أن لا يكونوا مخلوقين باليدين، ولا يشك في أنهم مخلوقون بالقدرة. وذلك يقتضي أن تكون اليد شيئاً سوى القدرة.
And as for His statement, 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands?' (14): We say: Scholars have two opinions on it. The first opinion: Indeed the two hands are two attributes subsisting in the essence of God Most High. By them creation occurs in the manner of honor and selection, as in the case of Adam, peace be upon him. And the proponents of this view adduced proofs: First: Indeed His statement, 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands?' indicates that God Most High made Adam prostrated to by the angels only because He created him with His two hands. So if 'hand' were an expression for power, then the cause of this prostration-worthiness would be present in all creatures, and this ruling would be necessary for all. And since it does not obtain, we know that 'hand' is an attribute other than power. Second: Indeed the power of God Most High is one, while 'hand' is described with duality. Third: Indeed His statement (Most High): 'When I created with My two hands' indicates that he is specifically created, and specification by mention indicates the negation of the ruling from what is other than it. So it is necessary that everyone other than Adam, peace be upon him, is not created with two hands, and there is no doubt that they are created with power. And that necessitates that 'hand' is something other than power.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument: Razi presents the first interpretation of the verse 'what I created with My two hands' (Qur'an 38:75). He states that some scholars hold that 'the two hands' are real attributes of God, by which He specially created Adam as an honor. He then provides three proofs from the text. The first proof: If 'hand' meant power, then all creatures would be equally worthy of prostration, but Adam alone is singled out, so 'hand' must mean something else. The second proof: God's power is singular, but 'hand' is dual, indicating a distinction. The third proof: The specification of Adam as created 'with My two hands' implies that others are not, so 'hand' cannot be power which is universal. Each proof is scripturally grounded.

Key Terms
اليدين
الصفة
القدرة
التثنية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'hand' in scripture is always metaphorical and never refers to a real attribute of God.
Correction: This passage argues that the verse's specifics indicate that 'hand' is a real attribute distinct from power, at least in this interpretive tradition.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof for the first opinion, why can 'hand' not mean power?
A) Because power is eternal, while hands are temporal.
B) Because if 'hand' meant power, all creatures would be equally worthy of prostration, but only Adam is.
C) Because the word 'hand' appears in dual form, which cannot describe power.
D) Because God's power is one, but hands are two.

Key Takeaway
The first opinion holds that God's hands are real attributes, distinct from power, proven by the verse's specificity, duality, and exclusivity to Adam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God's hands are real attributes, not just metaphors? If so, how does that change the way you read every verse about God's actions? Commit now to pause and reflect on each attribute verse you encounter this week, asking yourself: 'Do I accept this as real, or do I explain it away?'
?
When you read that Adam was created 'with My two hands', do you feel the weight of being honored by God? Or do you read it carelessly? What would it mean for you to live today fully aware that you are a direct creation of the One whose hands are real? Write one concrete way you will respond to that honor before you close this lesson.

Second Opinion: 'Hand' as Divine Power (Qudra)
Razi enumerates three proofs for equating 'hand' with power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's second interpretation equating 'hand' with divine power and the three proofs he uses to support it.

Core Idea
God's 'hand' is His power, proven by definition, necessity, and the absence of evidence.

In this passage, Imam al-Razi presents the second major interpretation of the divine attribute 'hand': that it refers to God's power (qudra). He offers three distinct proofs to show that no separate attribute beyond power is needed to account for creation. This moves us from metaphorical literalism to a precise theological identification rooted in rational necessity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the three numbered proofs (الوجه الأول, الثاني, الثالث).
The passage is structured as an enumeration of arguments.
2
Understand the first proof (definitional)
The first proof argues from the definition of power (qudra) and the common usage of 'hand' in Arabic. Both share the same meaning: ability to originate and bring into existence.
This is a lexical-linguistic argument.
3
Analyze the second proof (theological)
The second proof builds on the nature of God's power: it is eternal and must encompass all possible objects. If a separate attribute were needed for Adam's creation, it would require two independent agents on one effect—logically impossible.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Examine the third proof (methodological)
The third proof invokes the principle that no divine attribute may be affirmed without evidence. Since there is no proof for a distinct 'hand' attribute separate from power, it cannot be affirmed.
This uses the principle of consensus and evidence-based theology.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider how identifying 'hand' with power preserves tawhid and avoids the problem of multiple agents. Also note that this does not deny the attribute of power itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقول الثاني: إن اليد ههنا هي القدرة. ويدل عليه وجوه: الأول: إن القدرة عبارة عن الصفة التي يكون الموصوف بها متمكناً من الإيجاد والتكوين، ونقل الشيء من العدم إلى الوجود. ولما كان المسمى باليد كذلك، كان ذلك المعنى نفس القدرة. والثاني: إن قدرة الله تعالى صفة قديمة، واجبة الوجود، فيجب تعلقها بكل ما يصح أن يكون مقدوراً. وإلا لزم افتقارها في ذلك الاختصاص إلى المخصص. لكن المخصص (١٦) للمقدورية هو الإمكان، وهذا يقتضي أن يكون كل ممكن مقدوراً لله تعالى. ولا شك أن وجود آدم عليه السلام من الممكنات، فيكون وجود آدم من جملة متعلقات قدرة الله تعالى. فلو فرضنا صفة (١٧) أخرى مستقلة بإيجاد هذا الممكن، لزم أن يجتمع على الأثر الواحد مؤثران مستقلان وذلك محال. الثالث: إن إثبات صفة مؤثرة في وجود آدم، مما لا دليل على ثبوتها، ولا يجوز إثباتها؛ لانعقاد الإجماع على أن إثبات صفة من صفات الله تعالى من غير دليل لا يجوز.
And the second opinion: Indeed 'hand' here is power. And there are proofs indicating it: First: Indeed power is the attribute by which the one described is able to originate and bring into being, and to transfer a thing from non-existence to existence. And since what is called 'hand' is like that, then that meaning is the very same as power. Second: Indeed the power of God Most High is an eternal attribute, necessary of existence, so it must be related to everything that can possibly be an object of power. Otherwise, it would need a particularizer for that specification. But the particularizer (16) for objects of power is possibility, and this necessitates that every possible thing is an object of power for God Most High. And there is no doubt that the existence of Adam, peace be upon him, is among the possible things, so Adam's existence is among the things related to God's power. So if we were to assume another attribute (17) independent in bringing this possible into existence, then two independent agents would have to converge on a single effect, and that is impossible. Third: Indeed proving an effective attribute in the existence of Adam, for which there is no proof of its existence, is not permissible to prove; because there is consensus that proving an attribute of God's attributes without proof is not permissible.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents the second opinion: that 'hand' in the verse means divine power (qudra). Razi gives three proofs. The first proof defines power as the ability to create, and since 'hand' is used in the same context, it must be synonymous with power. The second proof is theological: God's power is eternal and must encompass all possibles. If Adam's creation required a special attribute beyond power, there would be two independent agents, which is impossible. The third proof relies on a methodological principle: attributes cannot be affirmed without evidence; since there is no evidence for a separate 'hand' attribute, it must be identified with power.

Key Terms
القدرة
الإمكان
المخصص
المقدور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that interpreting 'hand' as power denies the attribute of power or reduces God's attributes to a single one.
Correction: The interpretation does not deny God's attributes; it identifies a specific attribute (power) as the referent of 'hand'. Power remains a real and distinct attribute. The point is that no separate 'hand' attribute beyond power exists.

Checkpoint
What is the main argument of the second proof for the second opinion?
A) Power is an eternal attribute, so it must encompass all possibles, and any separate attribute would create two agents.
B) The word 'hand' never appears in the plural for God, so it must be singular in meaning.
C) Adam was created by a special act of power, not by a separate hand.
D) The consensus of scholars is that 'hand' means power.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Razi argues that 'hand' in the Qur'an refers to God's power, supported by definition, theological necessity, and the principle that attributes require proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on God's power encompassing every possible thing—including your own existence—do you truly live as though no other force or person has ultimate control over your life? What would change if you internalized that nothing happens except through His power?
?
The third proof warns against affirming attributes of God without evidence. Are there beliefs you hold about God or religion that you have never examined with evidence from revelation or reason? Will you commit to questioning one of them today?
?
Razi argues that if a separate attribute were needed for Adam's creation, two agents would converge on one effect—an absurdity. In your own life, do you sometimes act as though there are 'co-creators' with God, attributing outcomes to your own effort or luck rather than His sole power? How can you train your heart to see only His hand in every result?

Refutation of the First Proof: Hands and Honor
Refutation of the first proof of the first opinion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's method of refuting the claim that 'hands' in Adam's creation implies a special honor by demonstrating that the same phrase is used for animals and offering an alternative interpretation of care.

Core Idea
If hands meant honor, animals would be more honored than Adam.

Razi begins his response by tackling the first proof head-on. He shows that the opponents' logic would lead to an absurd conclusion: animals created by God's hands would be more honored than Adam. Then he provides a reasonable alternative: 'hands' here signifies God's special attention and care, not literal appendages.

Guided Path
1
Read the first response
Read the Arabic passage for the first proof refutation and its translation. Notice how Razi uses the Quranic verse about animals to turn the argument around.
2
Analyze the counterargument
Understand the logical structure: if A implies B, and A is also true for animals, then B would apply to animals. Since B does not apply to animals (they are not honored like Adam), the implication is false.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Examine the alternative interpretation
Razi suggests that 'hands' means special care. Note how he supports this with human language usage.
The alternative is plausible and avoids anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن القول (١٨) الأول: أما ما تمسكوا به أولاً: فهو أنه لو كان تخليق آدم باليدين يوجب مزيد الاصطفاء، لكان تخليق البهائم والأنعام بالأيدي يوجب رجحانها على آدم في هذا الاصطفاء، لقوله تعالى في صفة تخليقها: «مما عملت أيدينا أنعاماً فهم لها مالكون» (١٩). ثم نقول: لم لا يجوز أن يكون معنى قوله تعالى: «خلقت بيدي» هو بيان كثرة عناية الله تعالى في إيجاده وتكوينه. فإن الإنسان إذا أراد المبالغة في إصلاح بعض المهمات، وفي تكميله، فقد يقول: هذا الشيء أعملته بيدي. ومن المعلوم أن التخليق بغير هذا النوع من العناية ما كان حاصلاً في حق غير آدم عليه السلام. والجواب عما تمسكوا به ثانياً: إن التثنية لا تدل على حصول العدد، بدليل: قوله تعالى: «فقدموا بين يدي نجواكم صدقة» (٢٠). وقوله: «بين يدي رحمته» (٢١). والجواب عما تمسكوا به ثالثاً: إن التخصيص بالذكر هنا لم يدل
And the response to the first (18) opinion: As for what they adduced first: It is that if the creation of Adam with two hands necessitated greater selection, then the creation of beasts and cattle with hands would necessitate their superiority over Adam in this selection, because of His statement describing their creation: 'From what Our hands have made, cattle, and they are their owners' (19). Then we say: Why is it not permissible that the meaning of His statement 'I created with My two hands' is an expression of the abundance of God's care in His origination and formation? For a person, when he intends exaggeration in fixing some important matters and in perfecting them, may say: 'I worked this thing with my own hand.' And it is known that creation without this type of care did not occur in the case of anyone other than Adam, peace be upon him. And the response to what they adduced second: Indeed duality does not indicate the occurrence of number, as evidenced by His statement: 'Present charity before your hands' (20) and His statement: 'Before the hands of His mercy' (21). And the response to what they adduced third: Indeed specification by mention here does not indicate
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage contains Razi's refutation of the three proofs of the first opinion. He responds to the first proof by turning the argument: if creation by hands implies special honor, then animals created by 'Our hands' (Qur'an 36:71) would be more honored. He then offers an alternative interpretation: 'hands' here means special care, like a person saying 'I did it with my own hands' to emphasize effort. To the second proof, he argues that duality in Arabic does not necessarily imply numerical two, citing Quranic verses where 'yaday' means 'before' or 'presence' non-literally. To the third proof, he begins to argue that specification by mention does not imply negation elsewhere, but the text cuts off. Razi consistently uses scriptural examples to show the metaphorical usage of 'hand'.

Key Terms
الاصطفاء
العناية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'I created with My two hands' must be understood literally as Allah having two hands.
Correction: Razi shows that literal understanding leads to absurdity and that a metaphorical interpretation of 'special care' is plausible and supported by Quranic usage.

Checkpoint
What is the main flaw Razi identifies in the first proof?
A) It contradicts other Quranic verses about animals.
B) It assumes 'hands' must be literal.
C) It fails to consider that animals are also created by hands.
D) It ignores the metaphor of care.

Key Takeaway
Razi refutes the first proof by arguing that if hands meant honor, animals would be more honored, and instead interprets 'hands' as God's special care.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Refutation of the Second Proof: Duality and Number
Refutation of the second proof of the first opinion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that the dual form in Arabic does not necessarily indicate numerical two, especially when used of God.

Core Idea
Duality in Arabic often means 'presence,' not 'two.'

The second proof relied on the dual form 'yadayya' to assert that Allah has two hands. Razi counters by citing Quranic verses where the same dual form is used in contexts clearly not indicating numeral two, such as 'before your hands' meaning 'before you'.

Guided Path
1
Read the second response
Read the Arabic passage for the second proof refutation and its translation. Notice the Quranic verses cited.
2
Understand the linguistic argument
Razi claims that the dual form does not always imply number. In Arabic, 'yaday' can be idiomatic.
This is a common linguistic phenomenon.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Look at the two verses: 'before your hands' and 'before the hands of His mercy'. Note how 'yaday' means 'before' or 'presence'.
These examples show non-literal usage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن القول (١٨) الأول: أما ما تمسكوا به أولاً: فهو أنه لو كان تخليق آدم باليدين يوجب مزيد الاصطفاء، لكان تخليق البهائم والأنعام بالأيدي يوجب رجحانها على آدم في هذا الاصطفاء، لقوله تعالى في صفة تخليقها: «مما عملت أيدينا أنعاماً فهم لها مالكون» (١٩). ثم نقول: لم لا يجوز أن يكون معنى قوله تعالى: «خلقت بيدي» هو بيان كثرة عناية الله تعالى في إيجاده وتكوينه. فإن الإنسان إذا أراد المبالغة في إصلاح بعض المهمات، وفي تكميله، فقد يقول: هذا الشيء أعملته بيدي. ومن المعلوم أن التخليق بغير هذا النوع من العناية ما كان حاصلاً في حق غير آدم عليه السلام. والجواب عما تمسكوا به ثانياً: إن التثنية لا تدل على حصول العدد، بدليل: قوله تعالى: «فقدموا بين يدي نجواكم صدقة» (٢٠). وقوله: «بين يدي رحمته» (٢١). والجواب عما تمسكوا به ثالثاً: إن التخصيص بالذكر هنا لم يدل
And the response to the first (18) opinion: As for what they adduced first: It is that if the creation of Adam with two hands necessitated greater selection, then the creation of beasts and cattle with hands would necessitate their superiority over Adam in this selection, because of His statement describing their creation: 'From what Our hands have made, cattle, and they are their owners' (19). Then we say: Why is it not permissible that the meaning of His statement 'I created with My two hands' is an expression of the abundance of God's care in His origination and formation? For a person, when he intends exaggeration in fixing some important matters and in perfecting them, may say: 'I worked this thing with my own hand.' And it is known that creation without this type of care did not occur in the case of anyone other than Adam, peace be upon him. And the response to what they adduced second: Indeed duality does not indicate the occurrence of number, as evidenced by His statement: 'Present charity before your hands' (20) and His statement: 'Before the hands of His mercy' (21). And the response to what they adduced third: Indeed specification by mention here does not indicate

This passage contains Razi's refutation of the three proofs of the first opinion. Refutation of the Third Proof: Specification and Restriction
Beginning of refutation of the third proof of the first opinion.

Mentioning 'hands' does not mean no other attributes were involved.

The third proof argued that the specific mention of 'hands' in Adam's creation indicates a special status limited to that attribute. Razi begins his response by stating that specification by mention does not imply negation elsewhere, but the text cuts off, leaving the full argument incomplete.

Razi asserts that specifying something does not negate other things. For example, mentioning 'hands' does not mean other attributes were not involved.
This is a common theological principle.
3

The full argument is missing. We only have the beginning.

Imam Razi's Interpretation of Hadith on God's Hand
Imam Razi interprets hadith on God's hand and gives four logical proofs for metaphorical interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi interprets hadiths mentioning God's hand and why he argues that metaphorical interpretation is necessary based on four logical proofs.

Core Idea
Imam Razi shows that literal reading of God's hand leads to absurdities, so ta'wil is required.

Imam al-Razi tackles anthropomorphic hadiths about God's hand by first providing figurative interpretations consistent with divine transcendence. He then offers four compelling proofs that a literal understanding is impossible, demonstrating the necessity of metaphorical interpretation (ta'wil). This lesson examines both his interpretive method and his rational arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the flow of Razi's argument.
2
Identify the hadiths and interpretations
Notice how Razi explains each hadith mentioning 'hand' in a metaphorical sense—honor, mercy, care, power.
These interpretations are the first layer of his argument.
3
Analyze the four proofs
Examine each of the four proofs Razi gives against a literal reading of 'Charity falls into the hand of the Merciful'.
These proofs rely on sensory observation, Qur'anic consistency, and logical impossibility.
4
Reflect on the principle of ta'wil
Consider why Razi concludes that such texts must be interpreted metaphorically to uphold divine transcendence.
This principle is central in Islamic theology for dealing with ambiguous verses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الأحاديث فنقول: أما قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: خلق آدم بيده، وكتب التوراة بيده، فذلك حق يدل على أن المراد: التخصيص بمزيد الكرامات. وكذا قوله: كتب بيده على نفسه أن رحمتي سبقت غضبي. وأما قوله: إن الله يفتح أبواب السماء في ثلث الليل الباقي فيبسط يده، فالمراد: إفاضة النعمة، وإيصال الرحمة والمغفرة إلى المحتاجين. وأما قوله: الصدقة تقع في يد الرحمن، فالمراد منه: شدة العناية بقبول تلك الصدقات، وتكثير الثواب عليها. وكذا المراد بقوله عليه السلام: خمر طينة آدم بيده. وأما قوله عليه السلام: والذي نفسي بيده، فالمراد باليد هنا القدرة. والذي يدل على أن هذه الألفاظ يجب تأويلها: أن قوله الصدقة تقع في يد الرحمن، ليس المراد منه اليد بمعنى العضو والجارحة. ويدل عليه وجوه: الأول: إنا نشاهد أن تلك الصدقة ما وقعت إلا في يد الفقير. فالقول بأنها وقعت في يد أخرى، في عضو مركب من الأجزاء والأبعاض، مع أنا لا نراها ولا نحس بها، تشكيك في الضروريات. الثاني: هذا يقتضي أن تكون يد الله ظرفاً لصدقات العباد. وذلك خلاف ظاهر قوله تعالى: بل يداه مبسوطتان. الثالث: إن ذلك يقتضي أن تكون يد المعطي فوق يد المعبود، حتى يمكنه أن يوقع الصدقة في يد الرحمن، وذلك مناقض لظاهر قوله تعالى: يد الله فوق أيديهم. الرابع: إن ذلك يقتضي أن يكون هو على العرش، ويده على الأرض. وذلك لا يقوله عاقل. فثبت: أنه لابد في هذه الظواهر من التأويلات. وبالله التوفيق.
As for the hadiths, we say: Regarding his saying, peace be upon him, 'He created Adam with His hand, and wrote the Torah with His hand,' that is true and indicates that the intended meaning is specification with additional honors. Likewise his saying, 'He wrote with His hand upon Himself that My mercy precedes My anger.' As for his saying, 'Indeed Allah opens the doors of heaven in the last third of the night and spreads His hand,' the intended meaning is the outpouring of grace and the delivery of mercy and forgiveness to the needy. As for his saying, 'Charity falls into the hand of the Merciful,' the intended meaning is the intensity of care in accepting those charities and multiplying the reward for them. Similarly intended by his saying, peace be upon him, 'He kneaded the clay of Adam with His hand.' As for his saying, peace be upon him, 'By Whose hand my soul is,' the intended meaning of 'hand' here is power. What indicates that these expressions must be interpreted metaphorically is that his saying 'Charity falls into the hand of the Merciful' does not intend the hand in the sense of a bodily limb and organ. This is supported by proofs: First: we observe that that charity falls only into the hand of the poor person. So to claim that it fell into another hand—a limb composed of parts and sections—while we see it not nor perceive it, is a casting of doubt on necessities. Second: this would require that the hand of Allah be a container for the charities of servants, and that contradicts the apparent meaning of His statement, 'Nay, both His hands are outstretched.' Third: that would require that the hand of the giver be above the hand of the worshipped so that he can place the charity into the hand of the Merciful, and that contradicts the apparent meaning of His statement, 'The hand of Allah is above their hands.' Fourth: that would require that He be upon the Throne while His hand is upon the earth, and no rational person would say that. So it is established that these apparent meanings require metaphorical interpretation. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the necessity of metaphorical interpretation (ta'wil) for anthropomorphic expressions found in hadith. The author, Imam al-Razi, first addresses several hadiths that mention God's 'hand' (yad) and provides figurative interpretations for each. For the hadith 'He created Adam with His hand' and 'He wrote the Torah with His hand,' he explains that 'hand' here signifies special honor and distinction. Similarly, 'He wrote with His hand upon Himself' is interpreted as a figurative expression of mercy. The spreading of the hand in the night hadith is understood as the bestowal of grace and mercy. The hadith 'Charity falls into the hand of the Merciful' is interpreted as God's intense care and multiplication of reward. The hadith 'He kneaded the clay of Adam with His hand' follows the same pattern, and 'By Whose hand my soul is' is interpreted as 'power' (qudra). After these interpretations, al-Razi argues that such expressions cannot be taken literally, using the specific example of 'Charity falls into the hand of the Merciful.' He presents four logical proofs that a literal reading is impossible: First, we observe physically that charity only falls into the poor person's hand; claiming another unseen hand is a denial of sensory evidence. Second, if taken literally, it would require God's hand to be a spatial container for charity, contradicting the Qur'anic verse 'Both His hands are outstretched.' Third, it would imply the giver's hand is above God's hand, contradicting 'The hand of Allah is above their hands.' Fourth, it would entail God's hand being on earth while He is on the Throne, an absurd statement. He concludes that such texts must be interpreted metaphorically, seeking success from Allah. The author's method is to first harmonize hadith with rational necessity and clear Qur'anic verses, then provide decisive logical arguments against literalism.

Key Terms
يد (yad)
قدرة (qudra)
كرامات (karamat)
تأويل (ta'wil)
ظواهر (zawahir)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the early Muslims took these hadith literally without interpretation.
Correction: Imam al-Razi shows that even the apparent meaning requires ta'wil to avoid absurdities, and that the literal reading leads to contradictions with the Qur'an and reason.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi, what is the fourth proof against taking the hadith 'Charity falls into the hand of the Merciful' literally?
A) It would require God to have a physical hand composed of parts.
B) It would mean God's hand is a container for charity.
C) It would imply the giver's hand is above God's hand.
D) It would entail God being on the Throne while His hand is on earth.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Razi demonstrates through logical reasoning that anthropomorphic expressions in hadith must be interpreted metaphorically to preserve God's transcendence and avoid absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or hear hadith like 'the hand of Allah is above their hands,' do you feel any tension between the literal imagery and the belief that Allah is not a body? How does Razi's rational demonstration challenge you to refine your understanding?
?
Razi argues that claiming an unseen hand for God contradicts sensory evidence. Are you willing to submit your faith to such logical scrutiny, even if it means letting go of a cherished literal understanding that feels closer to piety?
?
Which of the four absurdities strikes you most personally? Does your heart instinctively resist the idea that Allah's hand could be a container or limited in space? What does that resistance teach you about what your heart already knows of Allah's majesty?

Al-Razi on the Term 'Qabdah': Evidence and Ta'wil
Al-Razi examines scriptural evidence for qabdah and explains its necessary ta'wil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the apparent meaning of 'qabdah' is impossible and how Al-Razi provides ta'wil for both the Qur'anic verse and the hadith reports.

Core Idea
When scripture describes Allah's 'grasp,' reason demands we interpret, not literalize.

This lesson examines a specific case of theological interpretation. Imam al-Razi presents the scriptural evidence for the term qabdah (grasp/handful) and then demonstrates why a literal reading leads to impossibility. He then offers a reasoned ta'wil (interpretation) that preserves both the scripture's authority and reason's integrity. By studying this passage, you will see how classical Sunni theologians reconciled apparent anthropomorphic language with divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the scriptural evidence
Read the Arabic passage where Al-Razi lists the Qur'anic verse and three hadith reports about qabdah. Notice the sources he cites (Ibn Khuzaymah).
The three hadiths are about Adam's creation and the two handfuls for Paradise and Hell.
2
Identify the problem with the apparent meaning
Al-Razi says the apparent meaning (zahir) is impossible (muhal). List the three reasons he gives: impurities, createdness, changeability.
These reasons are based on the earth's nature and the Creator's attributes.
3
Understand the ta'wil for the verse
Al-Razi explains that 'qabdah' in the verse means authority and dominion, not a literal grasp. He gives the example of 'the city in the grasp of the sultan.'
This is a common metaphorical usage in Arabic.
4
Understand the ta'wil for the hadith
Al-Razi explains that 'qabdah' in the hadith means a small amount (handful) of earth, a well-known metaphorical expression.
It is like saying 'a handful' to indicate a small quantity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل السابع عشر في إثبات القبضة

هذه اللفظة قد وردت في الأخبار والقرآن. أما القرآن فقوله تعالى: {والأرض جميعاً قبضته يوم القيامة} [الزمر:67]. وأما الأخبار فكثيرة: الخبر الأول: ما روى ابن خزيمة في كتابه الذي سماه "التوحيد" عن أبي موسى الأشعري رضي الله عنه عن النبي أنه قال: "إن الله خلق آدم من قبضة قبضها من جميع الأرض، فجاء بنو آدم على قدر الأرض، فجاء منهم الأحمر والأسود، والسهل والجبل، والخبيث والطيب". الخبر الثاني: ما روى ابن خزيمة في كتابه عن أنس بن مالك رضي الله عنه عن النبي: أن الله قبض قبضة وقال: "إلى الجنة برحمتي"، وقبض قبضة وقال: "إلى النار ولا أبالى". الخبر الثالث: عن أبي سعيد الخدري رضي الله عنه عن النبي في القبضتين: "هذه في الجنة ولا أبالى، وهذه في النار ولا أبالى".

واعلم أن ظاهر الآية يقتضي أن تكون الأرض قبضته. وذلك محال. لأن الأرض محتوية على النجاسات. فكيف يقول القائل: إنها قبضة إله العالم؟ ولأن القرآن مملوء من أن الأرض مخلوقة، وقبضة الخالق لا تكون مخلوقة. ولأن الأرض تقبل الاجتماع والافتراق والعمارة والتخريب، وقبضة الخالق لا تكون كذلك. فلا بد من التأويل. وهو أن يقال: إن الأرض في قبضته. إلا أن هذا الكلام كما يذكر ويراد به احتواء الأنامل على الشيء، فقد يذكر ويراد به كون الشيء في قدرته وتصرفه وملكه. يقال: هذه البلدة في قبضة السلطان. والمراد: ما ذكرناه. وأما القبضة المذكورة في الخبر فالمراد: أنه تعالى ميز من تراب الأرض مقدار القبضة. وهذا مجاز مشهور. يقال للشيء القليل: إنه قبضة وحفنة. والمراد: أن مقداره مثل ذلك. وبالله التوفيق.
Chapter Seventeen on Establishing the 'Qabdah' (Grasp/Handful)

This word has occurred in the reports and the Qur'an. As for the Qur'an, His saying, the Exalted: {And the earth entirely will be in His grasp on the Day of Resurrection} [Az-Zumar:67]. As for the reports, they are many: The first report: What was narrated by Ibn Khuzaymah in his book which he called "At-Tawhid", from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Prophet, that he said: "Indeed Allah created Adam from a handful which He seized from all of the earth. So the children of Adam came according to (the variation of) the earth; there came from them the red, the black, the easy, the difficult, the wicked, and the good." The second report: What was narrated by Ibn Khuzaymah in his book from Anas ibn Malik, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Prophet: that Allah seized a handful and said: "To Paradise by My mercy," and seized a handful and said: "To the Fire, and I do not care." The third report: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Prophet concerning the two handfuls: "This one is in Paradise and I do not care, and this one is in the Fire and I do not care."

Know that the apparent meaning of the verse necessitates that the earth be His grasp. But that is impossible, because the earth contains impurities. So how could one say that it is the grasp of the Lord of the worlds? And because the Qur'an is full of (the fact) that the earth is created, whereas the grasp of the Creator cannot be created. And because the earth admits of combination and separation, habitation and desolation, whereas the grasp of the Creator is not like that. So ta'wil (interpretation) is necessary. That is, to say: The earth is in His grasp. However, this word, as it is used and intended by it (the meaning of) containing a thing by the fingers, it may also be used and intended by it (the meaning of) a thing being in His power, disposal, and dominion. One says: "This city is in the grasp of the sultan." And the intended meaning is what we have mentioned. As for the (word) 'qabdah' mentioned in the report, the intended meaning is that He, the Exalted, separated a measure of a handful from the earth's soil. And this is a well-known metaphorical usage. It is said of a small thing: 'It is a handful and a fistful.' And the intended meaning is that its measure is like that. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about the attribute of 'qabdah' (grasp/handful) as it appears in the Qur'an and hadith. Al-Razi begins by presenting the textual evidence: the Qur'anic verse (Az-Zumar 67) stating that the earth will be in Allah's grasp, and three hadith reports from Ibn Khuzaymah's book 'At-Tawhid'. The first hadith describes Adam's creation from a handful taken from all the earth, leading to human diversity. The second and third hadiths refer to two handfuls: one for Paradise (by mercy) and one for the Fire (without care).

Having presented the evidence, Al-Razi then identifies a problem: the apparent (zahir) meaning of the verse implies that the earth itself is God's grasp, which is impossible (muhal). He provides three reasons: (1) the earth contains impurities, so it cannot be the grasp of the Lord of the worlds; (2) the earth is created, whereas the grasp of the Creator is uncreated; (3) the earth undergoes change (combination, separation, habitation, desolation), whereas the grasp of the Creator does not. Therefore, ta'wil (interpretation) is necessary.

Al-Razi then gives the ta'wil. For the verse, it means that the earth is in His grasp, i.e., under His power, disposal, and dominion — a metaphorical usage similar to saying "this city is in the grasp of the sultan." For the hadith, 'qabdah' means a handful (small amount) of earth, a well-known metaphorical expression (majaz mashhur) where a small quantity is called a 'qabdah' or 'hafnah'. The passage concludes with 'And with Allah is success.'

Key Terms
قبضة
تأويل
مجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'qabdah' implies Allah literally has a hand or grasp similar to created beings.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that the literal meaning is impossible and must be interpreted metaphorically as dominion (verse) or a small amount (hadith).

Checkpoint
Why does Al-Razi consider the apparent meaning of 'qabdah' in the verse impossible?
A) Because the earth is too large to be grasped.
B) Because the earth contains impurities, is created, and changeable.
C) Because the hadiths contradict the verse.
D) Because 'qabdah' only occurs in hadith, not the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
The term 'qabdah' in scripture must be interpreted metaphorically as dominion (for the verse) or a small amount (for the hadith) to avoid anthropomorphism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'the earth entirely will be in His grasp,' does your heart immediately imagine a physical hand? How does Al-Razi's threefold argument (impurities, createdness, change) challenge that assumption? Will you now actively remind yourself that Allah's grasp is unlike any creation, and what specific mental reminder can you use when you recite this verse in prayer?
?

After studying this passage, are you willing to accept ta'wil when reason demands it? Write down one specific verse about Allah's attributes that you have struggled to reconcile with reason, and commit to seeking its proper ta'wil from learned scholars before you recite it again.
?
The hadith mentions two handfuls—one for Paradise and one for the Fire—with the statement 'I do not care.' Does this challenge your understanding of Allah's justice? How does Al-Razi's explanation (that it refers to a small amount of earth, not a literal selection) reshape your view of divine decree and mercy? Ask yourself: Do I truly trust that Allah's mercy and justice are perfect, even when His actions seem severe to my limited mind?

Interpretation of the Attribute of Grasp (Qabdah)
Imam Razi explains the necessity of metaphorical interpretation for 'qabdah'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attribute 'qabdah' must be interpreted metaphorically and what meanings it carries.

Core Idea
Divine attributes like 'qabdah' must be understood metaphorically to avoid anthropomorphism.

Imam Razi addresses a key challenge: words like 'grasp' seem to imply a physical hand. He shows that such literal readings are impossible for Allah and that the Qur'anic and prophetic language uses well-established metaphorical usages to convey power, possession, or quantity. This passage exemplifies the method of ta'wil in preserving divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the problem
Notice why Imam Razi says literal interpretation is impossible: a physical grasp involves fingers and manipulation, which cannot apply to the Creator.
This is the starting point for ta'wil.
3
Examine the two metaphorical meanings
First, 'qabdah' can mean power and control, as in 'the city is in the grip of the sultan'. Second, in the hadith, it means a small quantity of earth, a well-known metaphor.
Both meanings are established in Arabic usage.
4
Reflect on divine transcendence
Ask yourself: how does this interpretation protect Allah from being compared to creation? This is the purpose of ta'wil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يذكر والعمارة والتخريب، وقبضة الخالق لا تكون كذلك. فإذا لابد من التأويل. وهو أن يقال: إن الأرض في قبضته. إلا أن هذا الكلام كما، ويراد به احتواء الأنامل على الشيء، فقد يذكر ويراد به كون الشيء في قدرته وتصرفه وملكه. يقال: هذه البلدة في قبضة السلطان. والمراد: ما ذكرناه. وأما القبضة المذكورة في الخبر فالمراد: أنه تعالى ميز من تراب الأرض مقدار القبضة. وهذا مجاز مشهور. يقال للشيء القليل: إنه قبضة وحفنة. والمراد: أن مقداره مثل ذلك. وبالله التوفيق.
It is mentioned, building and destruction, and the grasp of the Creator is not like that. So then interpretation is necessary. And it is that it is said: The earth is in His grasp. Except that this speech [؟], and by it is meant the enclosing of the fingers over the thing; so it may be mentioned and by it is meant the thing being in His power, disposal, and possession. As for the grasp mentioned in the report, the intended meaning is that He Almighty distinguished from the dust of the earth the measure of a handful. And this is a well-known metaphor. Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the correct interpretation of the attribute 'qabdah' (grasp or handful) attributed to Allah. The author begins by stating that the literal meaning of 'qabdah' as a physical grasp involving fingers is impossible for the Creator. Therefore, interpretation (ta'wil) is necessary. One common interpretation is that 'the earth is in His grasp' means that it is under His power and control, just as one says 'this city is in the grip of the sultan' to denote possession and authority. However, the author then addresses the specific hadith that mentions a 'qabdah' (handful) of earth. He explains that this refers to Allah distinguishing a small quantity of earth, and it is a well-known metaphor where a 'handful' is used to denote a small amount. Thus, the passage emphasizes the necessity of metaphorical interpretation (majaz) for anthropomorphic expressions to preserve divine transcendence.

The Anthropomorphist Proofs for Two Hands
Razi enumerates the anthropomorphist proofs from Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic and hadith evidence that anthropomorphists use to claim literal two hands for Allah.

Core Idea
Anthropomorphists cite Quran and hadith to claim Allah has literal hands.

Imam Razi begins this chapter by presenting the arguments of those who insist on taking the attribute of 'hands' literally. He cites two Quranic verses and a detailed hadith. This lesson examines these proofs as they appear in his text, before his refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the evidence types
Read the Arabic passage once to see the overall structure: first Quranic verses, then a hadith. Notice the author's framing: 'They argued with the Quran and the reports.'
The passage is a presentation of opposing views, not Razi's own position.
2
Examine the two Quranic verses
Look at the verses: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands?' (38:75) and 'But His two hands are outstretched' (5:64). Ask: How do these verses support a literal interpretation?
Anthropomorphists take 'beyond' and 'outstretched' as describing physical hands.
3
Analyze the hadith for details reinforcing literal hands
The hadith mentions 'His two hands were clenched' and 'both His hands are right, blessed'. Identify how these phrases suggest physical movement and distinction between right and left.
The hadith is long; only the relevant portion is quoted. The author notes this.
4
Connect to the broader debate
Consider why Razi presents these proofs. He will later refute them. This lesson sets up the opposing view.

الفصل الثامن عشر في ما تمسكوا به في اثبات اليدين لله عز وجل. احتجوا بالقرآن، والأخبار. أما القرآن: فقوله تعالى: ( ما منعك أن تسجد لما خلقت بيدي )؟ وقوله تعالى: ( بل يداه مبسوطتان ). وأما الخبر: فما روى ابن خزيمة عن أبي هريرة ( رضي الله عنه ) قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم: « لما خلق الله آدم ونفخ فيه: عطس. فقال: الحمد لله، فحمد الله، بإذن الله. فقال له ربه: يرحمك ربك يا آدم. ثم قال له: يا آدم اذهب إلى الملائكة فقل: السلام عليكم. فلما ذهب وقال: قالوا: عليكم السلام ورحمة الله. ثم رجع إلى ربه. فقال: هذه تحيتك وتحية بنيك وبنيهم. فقال الله تعالى - ويداه مقبوضتان - اختر أيهما شئت. فقال: اخترت يمين ربي - وكلتا يديه يمين مباركة - ثم بسطها فإذا فيها آدم وذريته. فقال: أي رب ما هؤلاء؟ فقال: هؤلاء ذريتك، فإذا كل إنسان مكتوب عمره بين عينيه. واعلم: أن هذا الحديث طويل. ومقصودنا هنا: هذا القدر. وقد
Chapter eighteen: On what they hold onto in proving the two hands for Allah Almighty. They argued with the Quran and the reports. As for the Quran: His saying: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands?' And His saying: 'But His two hands are outstretched.' As for the report: That which Ibn Khuzayma narrated from Abu Huraira (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family) said: 'When Allah created Adam and breathed into him, he sneezed. He said: Praise be to Allah, so he praised Allah by Allah's permission. His Lord said to him: Your Lord has mercy on you, O Adam. Then He said: O Adam, go to the angels and say: Peace be upon you. When he went and said: They said: Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah. Then he returned to his Lord. He said: This is your greeting and the greeting of your children and their children. Then Allah said - and His two hands were clenched - choose whichever you wish. Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a presentation of the anthropomorphist arguments for the existence of literal 'two hands' for Allah. The author, Imam Razi, structures it as a chapter heading followed by two types of evidence: Quranic verses and a hadith. First, he cites two Quranic verses: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands?' (38:75) and 'But His two hands are outstretched' (5:64). These are commonly used by those who take the attribute of 'hands' literally. Then he presents a lengthy hadith from Ibn Khuzayma via Abu Huraira, which describes Adam's creation, his greeting of the angels, and then Allah showing Adam his offspring with their lifespans written, using the phrase 'His two hands were clenched' and 'He chose My right hand'. The hadith explicitly mentions 'both His hands are right, blessed'. The author notes that only the relevant portion is quoted, as the full hadith is long. The passage ends abruptly with 'وقد' (and), indicating continuation on the next page. This evidence is presented as the basis for the claim of literal hands, which Razi will likely refute in subsequent discussion.

Proofs for Affirming Allah's Right Hand
Imam Razi cites Quran and hadith to prove the attribute of Yamin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic and hadith evidence used by Imam Razi to affirm the attribute of Yamin (Right Hand) for Allah.

Core Idea
The Quran and Sunnah affirm Allah's Right Hand, but without anthropomorphism or denial.

Imam Razi opens a new chapter dedicated to proving the divine attribute of Yamin (Right Hand) through scriptural sources. He first cites two Quranic verses that explicitly mention Allah's right hand, then presents three hadiths from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that reinforce this attribute. As you read, note that these texts are presented as evidence, not as an invitation to imagine a physical limb.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overanalysis. Then read the full English translation to grasp the flow of evidence.
The passage is a clear enumeration of proofs.
2
Identify the Quranic proofs
Locate the two Quranic verses cited. Note their references and what they say about Allah's right hand.
Az-Zumar 67 and Al-Haqqah 45.
3
Examine the first two hadiths
Look at the hadith that says 'Both His hands are right' and the hadith about Allah seizing the earth and folding the heavens with His right hand.
These emphasize the comprehensiveness and power of Allah's right hand.
4
Study the third hadith about Adam
Consider the long hadith about Allah creating Adam and bringing forth his progeny with His right hand, distinguishing those for Paradise and Hell.
This hadith ties the attribute to divine decree.
5
Reflect on the purpose of these proofs
Understand that Imam Razi is providing textual evidence, but the Salaf accept these attributes without ta'til (denial) or tashbih (comparison).
The passage does not delve into interpretation; it only presents the proof texts.

The Nineteenth Chapter: On Affirming the Right Hand (Yamin) for Allah. They adduced (against him?) the Quran and the reports. As for the Quran, His statement Most High: 'And the heavens are folded in His Right Hand' (39:67), and His statement: 'We would have seized him by the right hand' (69:45). Then He wiped his back and brought forth from him offspring, and said: I created these for the Fire, and with the deeds of the people of the Fire they will act.'

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a new chapter that provides textual evidence for affirming the attribute of Yamin (Right Hand) for Allah. These texts are proof that the attribute 'Yamin' is affirmed, but according to the methodology of the Salaf, they are accepted without ta'til (denial) or tashbih (anthropomorphism).

Evidence for Allah's Yameen from Qur'an and Hadith
Qur'anic and hadith evidence for yameen

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Qur'anic verses and prophetic hadith that are cited as evidence for affirming the attribute of yameen (right hand) for Allah.

Core Idea
The Qur'an and hadith affirm Allah's yameen, but its meaning requires careful interpretation.

Imam Razi begins by presenting the scriptural proofs that opponents of tanzih often use to argue for a literal hand. He quotes two Qur'anic verses and four hadith reports. These texts are the foundation for the discussion, but as we will see in the next lesson, their true meaning points to power, not a limb.

Guided Path
1
Read the passages carefully
Read the Arabic text once, then the translation. Notice that the first part is the chapter heading and the second part presents the evidences from Qur'an and hadith in order.
There are two Qur'anic verses and four hadith reports. Identify each one.
2
Identify the evidences
List the two Qur'anic verses and the four hadith reports. For each hadith, note the narrator and a brief summary.
The hadith include: (1) 'Both His hands are right,' (2) Allah grasping the earth and folding the heavens, (3) creation of Adam and predestination, (4) charity placed in Allah's right hand.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why Imam Razi lists these evidences. Are they proof of a literal hand or something else? This will be answered in the next lesson.

في
إثبات اليمين لله تعالى

احتجوا عليه بالقرآن والأخبار.

أما القرآن: فقوله تعالى: "والسموات مطويات بيمينه" وقوله: "لأخذنا منه باليمين".

وأما الأخبار فكثيرة:
الأول: قوله عليه السلام: "كلتا يديه يمين".
والثاني: عن أبي هريرة أنه قال: قال رسول الله: "يقبض الله الأرض يوم القيامة، ويطوي السموات بيمينه، ثم يقول: أنا الملك، فأين ملوك الأرض؟".
والثالث: روى صاحب شرح السنة في باب "الإيمان بالقدر" عن عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه قال: سمعت النبي يقول: "إن الله خلق آدم، ثم مسح ظهره بيمينه، ثم استخرج منه ذرية فقال: خلقت هؤلاء للجنة، وبعمل أهل الجنة يعملون. ثم مسح ظهره فاستخرج منه ذرية فقال: خلقت هؤلاء للنار، وبعمل أهل النار يعملون".
والرابع: روى ابن خزيمة في كتابه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم قال: "إن أحدكم يتصدق بالتمرة من كسب طيب – ولا يقبل الله إلا طيبا – فيجعلها في يده اليمين، ثم يربيها كما يربي أحدكم فلوه وفصيله، حتى يصير مثل أحد".

واعلم: أن اليمين عبارة عن القوة والقدرة. والدليل عليه: أنه الجانب الأيمن سمي باليمين لأنه أقوى الجانبين، وسمي الخلف باليمين لأنه يقوى عزم الإنسان على الفعل أو الترك. قال الشاعر:
إذا ما راية رفعت لمجد
تلقاها عرابة باليمين

إذا عرفت هذا فنقول: ظهر الوجه في قوله تعالى: "والسموات مطويات بيمينه". وأما قوله تعالى: "لأخذنا منه باليمين" فالمراد منه يمين المأخوذ أي أخذنا بيمين ذلك الإنسان، وهو كأن يقال: أخذت بيمين الصبي وذهبت به إلى المكتب. وإن كان المراد يمين الآخذ فالمراد منه القوة والقدرة. وإذا عرفت ذلك في الآية فاعرف مثله في الأخبار.
Chapter Nineteen: On Affirming al-Yameen for Allah Almighty. They argued against it with the Qur'an and the reports. As for the Qur'an: His saying, the Most High: 'And the heavens are folded in His right hand (yameenih),' and His saying: 'We would have seized him by the right hand (al-yameen).' As for the reports, they are many: First: His saying, peace be upon him: 'Both of His hands are right.' Second: From Abu Huraira that he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Allah will grasp the earth on the Day of Resurrection, and fold the heavens with His right hand (yameenih), then say: I am the King. Where are the kings of the earth?' Third: The author of Sharh al-Sunna narrated in the chapter 'Faith in al-Qadar' from Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: I heard the Prophet say: 'Verily, Allah created Adam, then wiped his back with His right hand (yameenih), then extracted from him offspring and said: I created these for Paradise, and with the deeds of the people of Paradise they act. Then He wiped his back and extracted from him offspring and said: I created these for the Fire, and with the deeds of the people of the Fire they act.' Fourth: Ibn Khuzayma narrated in his book from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and his family and grant them peace, that he said: 'One of you gives charity with a date from a good earning – and Allah accepts only what is good – then He places it in His right hand (yameenih), then He raises it as one of you raises his foal and his young camel, until it becomes like Mount Uhud.' And know: that al-yameen is an expression for strength (al-quwwa) and power (al-qudra). And the evidence for it: that the right side (al-janib al-ayman) is called al-yameen because it is the stronger of the two sides, and the successor (al-khalaf) is called al-yameen because it strengthens (yuqawwi) a person's resolve to do or leave an action. The poet said: 'Whenever a banner is raised for honor, 'Araba receives it with the right hand (yameen).' If you know this, then we say: The meaning appears in His saying, the Most High: 'And the heavens are folded in His right hand (yameenih).' As for His saying, the Most High: 'We would have seized him by the right hand (al-yameen)' – the intended meaning is the right hand of the seized one, i.e., We seized that man by his right hand, analogous to saying: I took the boy by his right hand and took him to school. But if the intended meaning is the right hand of the seizer, then the intended meaning is strength and power. And if you understand that regarding the verse, then understand likewise regarding the reports.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument for affirming the attribute of 'al-Yameen' (the Right Hand) for Allah while interpreting it in a way that befits His transcendence. The author begins by stating that the opponents (likely anthropomorphists) argued using the Qur'an and hadith. He then presents the two Qur'anic verses: 'And the heavens are folded in His right hand' (az-Zumar 67) and 'We would have seized him by the right hand' (al-Haaqqa 45). Following that, he lists four prophetic hadith: the first stating that both of Allah's hands are right; the second describing Allah grasping the earth and folding the heavens with His right hand; the third narrating the creation of Adam and the predestination of his offspring to Paradise or Fire; and the fourth about charity being placed in Allah's right hand and nurtured. After presenting this evidence, the author provides the key interpretive move: 'al-yameen' is an expression for strength (quwwa) and power (qudra). He supports this linguistically by noting that the right side is called 'yameen' because it is stronger, and that the 'khalaf' (successor or back) is called 'yameen' because it strengthens resolve. He cites a line of poetry where 'yameen' clearly means power. Then he applies this interpretation: in the first verse, the meaning is the power of Allah; in the second verse, he offers two possibilities: either the 'yameen' belongs to the seized person (meaning his literal right hand) or, if attributed to the seizer, it means strength and power. He concludes that all reports should be understood similarly, i.e., metaphorically. The passage thus guards against anthropomorphism by affirming the wording but interpreting the meaning in a transcendent sense, consistent with the Sunni principle of tanzih.

Key Terms
اليمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many hadith reports does Imam Razi present in this passage?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi presents two Qur'anic verses and four hadith as the scriptural basis for affirming yameen, setting up the need for proper interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah takes your charity in His right hand and raises it until it becomes like a mountain, does that change how you view your small acts of giving? Will you now be more intentional about giving from a good earning, knowing that Allah values it so highly?
?
The hadith about Adam's offspring being created for Paradise or Fire can be unsettling. Do you trust Allah's wisdom and justice in predestination, or do you struggle with the idea that some are created for the Fire? What does this suggest about your heart's reliance on His mercy?
?
These texts affirm a 'right hand' for Allah, yet we know He is unlike His creation. When you encounter such descriptions, do you find yourself tempted to imagine a physical hand, or do you submit by saying 'we believe, we do not know how'? Which response brings more peace to your heart?

Interpreting Yameen as Power and Its Application
Linguistic interpretation of yameen as power

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and rational argument for interpreting yameen as strength and power, and how this applies to the scriptural proofs.

Core Idea
Yameen in Arabic means strength and power, not a limb.

In the previous lesson, we saw the scriptural evidence for yameen. Now Imam Razi provides the key interpretive principle: yameen is a word that denotes strength and power. He supports this with linguistic reasoning, a poetic citation, and then applies it to the Qur'anic verses and hadith reports. This is a classic example of tanzih — affirming the scriptural wording while negating any anthropomorphic meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the linguistic argument
Read the part starting from 'واعلم' to the end. Notice how Imam Razi connects the word yameen to the root meaning of strength.
He points out that the right side is stronger, and that 'khalaf' (successor) is called yameen because it strengthens resolve.
2
Examine the application to the verses
See how Imam Razi applies this interpretation to the two Qur'anic verses. For the first verse, he says the meaning is clear: it refers to Allah's power. For the second, he offers two possibilities.
Pay attention to the nuance: the yameen could belong to the seized person, or if to Allah, it means power.
3
Apply the same to the hadith
Imam Razi concludes that the same interpretation should be applied to all the hadith reports. Understand why this is necessary for maintaining tanzih.
This ensures that no anthropomorphic meaning is attached to the reports.

Second Objection: Implies Ignorance of God
Imam Razi gives the second proof that the hadith imply God's ignorance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the literal meaning of the hadith appears to imply that God lacked knowledge of the final numbers of people in Paradise and Hell, and how this serves as a rational objection requiring figurative interpretation.

Core Idea
A literal reading of the hadith suggests God did not know the final counts.

Imam Razi presents a second logical objection: if we take the hadith at face value, it suggests God did not know in advance how many people would enter Paradise or Hell. This directly contradicts the attribute of omniscience. Let's carefully trace his reasoning and see why the literal meaning cannot be correct.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the logical structure: hadith implies ignorance, therefore over-creation, therefore need for extra creation and God's foot.
The sequence is important for understanding the argument.
2
Identify the key implication
Identify the main claim: the hadith implies God was not knowledgeable of the measure of people of reward and punishment.
3
Understand the rational contradiction
Ask yourself: Why would creating too large a Paradise and Hell point to ignorance? Because an all-knowing Creator would create exactly the right size from the start.
This is the core of the objection.
4
Connect to the need for ta'wil
Realize that this impossibility forces us to interpret the hadith metaphorically, not literally. Imam Razi uses this as a proof that the literal meaning is false.
This shows how rational arguments are used in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني: إن هذا الحديث يقتضى أنه تعالى ما كان عالما بمقدار أهل الثواب والعقاب، فلا جرم خلق الله الجنة والنار أوسع من قدر الحاجة ولا جرم احتاج إلى أن يخلق للجنة خلقا آخر، وأن قدمه في النار.
Second: This hadith implies that He – exalted is He – was not knowledgeable of the measure of the people of reward and punishment, and therefore God created Paradise and Hell larger than the necessary capacity, and therefore He needed to create another creation for Paradise and to place His foot in Hell.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection against the literal interpretation of the hadith. Imam Razi argues that if we take the hadith at face value, it would mean that God did not know in advance how many people would enter Paradise and Hell. This is because the hadith says that Hell will not be filled until God places His foot in it, and Paradise will have extra space until God creates more people. If God already knew the exact numbers, He would have created them exactly the right size from the beginning. The fact that there is extra space and a need to fill it later implies that God's knowledge was incomplete – which is impossible for God. Therefore, the literal meaning cannot be correct.

Key Terms
عالما بمقدار
أهل الثواب والعقاب
أوسع من قدر الحاجة
يخلق للجنة خلقا آخر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the hadith simply describes a future event without implicating God's knowledge.
Correction: Imam Razi shows that the literal description logically implies God lacked foreknowledge of the final numbers, which is impossible for God.

Checkpoint
What does the second objection say the hadith wrongly implies about God?
A) That He is unjust
B) That He is not all-knowing
C) That He is unable to fill Hell
D) That He changes His mind

Key Takeaway
The second objection reveals that a literal reading of the hadith clashes with divine omniscience, proving it must be interpreted figuratively.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Would you have the courage to challenge them using the logic from this lesson, or would you remain silent to avoid conflict? What is at stake if you stay silent?

Divine Joy and Wonder: Metaphors for Divine Pleasure
Razi interprets hadiths about God's joy and wonder as metaphors for divine pleasure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi interprets scriptural attributions of joy and wonder to God as metaphorical expressions of divine approval and magnification.

Core Idea
God's 'joy' and 'wonder' are metaphors for His pleasure and magnification of deeds.

This passage from Razi's Asas al-Taqdis addresses two scriptural descriptions that seem to attribute human emotions to God: joy (farah) and wonder ('ajab). Razi explains that these are not literal emotions but rather metaphors for divine approval (rida) and the magnification of actions. Through careful interpretation, he shows how the language of the Quran and Hadith can be understood in a way befitting God's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the content sink in before you interpret.
Notice the two main topics: joy and wonder.
2
Identify the interpretation of joy
Find where Razi presents the hadith on repentance and welcoming, and note how he interprets 'joy' as a name for 'approval' (rida).
This is a key metaphorical move.
3
Identify the interpretation of wonder
Find the discussion of wonder, including the Qur'anic reading, and note how Razi interprets it as 'magnification' (isti'zam) of an act.
Wonder arises from magnifying something great.
4
Reflect on the overall approach
Consider why Razi uses metaphorical interpretation for these attributes. How does this preserve God's transcendence?
This is a standard kalam method for anthropomorphic expressions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثامن والعشرون فى الفرح عن النعمان بن بشير - رضي الله عنه ـ عن النبي الا أنه قال الله أفرح بتوبة العبد من العبد ، إذا ضلت راحلته في أرض فلاة في يوم قائظ ، و راحلته عليها زاده ومزاده. إذا ضلت ( راحلته أيقن بالهلاك) (1) وإذا وجدها ، فرح بذلك . فالله أشد فرحاً بتوبة عبده من هذ العبد ، وقال : ( لا يطأ الرجل المساجد للصلاة والذكر ، إلا تبشبش الله تعالى إليه ، ما يقتبشيش أهل الغائب بغائبهم ، إذا قدم عليهم ، والتأويل : هو أن من يرضى بالشيء يفرح به فيسمى الرضا : بالفرح . وهذا هو الكلام به. . في البشاشة . ومن هذا الباب قوله : ( عجب ربكم من شاب ليس له ما صبوة ، وفي حديث آخر : عجب ربكم من ثلاثة : القوم إذا اصطفوا في الصلاة ، والقوم إذا صلوا في قتال المشركين ، ورجل يقوم إلى الصلاة في جوف الليل، وقرأ : «بل عجبت و يسخرون» ـ بضم التاء - وذلك بدل على ثبوت هذا المعنى في حق الله تعالى . واعلم : أن التأويل هو : أن التعجب حالة تحصل عند استعظام الأمر . فإذا عظم الله تعالى فعلا ، إما في كثرة ثوابه أو فى كثرة عقابه ، جاز إطلاق لفظ التعجب عليه (و بالله التوفيق ) (۲)
The twenty-eighth chapter on joy: From al-Nu'man ibn Bashir (may Allah be pleased with him) from the Prophet (ﷺ) that he said: 'Allah is more joyful at the repentance of a servant than a man whose riding beast is lost in a barren land on a scorching day, and his beast carries his provisions and his water-skin. When his riding beast is lost, he is certain of destruction, and when he finds it, he rejoices. So Allah is more intensely joyful at the repentance of His servant than this man.' And He said: 'No man treads the mosques for prayer and remembrance except that Allah Most High welcomes him, more than the family of an absent one welcomes their absent when he returns to them.' The interpretation: it is that whoever is pleased with something rejoices at it, so approval is called 'joy'. And this is the speech about alacrity. From this same category is His saying: 'Your Lord wonders at a young man who has no youthful passion.' And in another hadith: 'Your Lord wonders at three: people who line up in prayer, people who pray while fighting the polytheists, and a man who gets up for prayer in the depth of the night.' And He recited: 'Rather, I am amazed, and they mock,' with damma on the ta. That indicates the affirmation of this meaning with respect to Allah Most High. Know that the interpretation is: wonder is a state that occurs when magnifying a matter. So if Allah Most High magnifies an act, whether for the abundance of its reward or for the abundance of its punishment, it is permissible to apply the term 'wonder' to Him. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal interpretation of scriptural texts that attribute joy (farah) and wonder ('ajab) to God. The author first presents two hadiths: one comparing God's joy at repentance to a man finding his lost beast, and another about God welcoming those who frequent mosques. He then gives the interpretation: joy is a metaphor for divine approval (rida), because one who is pleased rejoices. He then extends this to the concept of 'bishasha' (alacrity). Next, he addresses hadiths about God's wonder, including the Qur'anic reading 'bal 'ajibtu' (with dammah). He explains that wonder is a state arising from magnifying something; thus, when God magnifies an act—whether for great reward or great punishment—the term 'wonder' can be applied metaphorically to Him. The passage systematically shows that these terms do not imply literal emotions in God but are expressions of His pleasure or magnification of deeds.

Correction: Razi explains that these are metaphors for divine approval and magnification, not literal emotions.

D) As a statement about the mosque's spiritual rewards.

Key Takeaway
Razi interprets scriptural references to God's joy and wonder as metaphors for divine pleasure and magnification, preserving God's transcendence.
